71.   Expected Outputs. The following are the expected outputs at the end of project's implementation:
(i) economic and labor market information provided to individuals and human capital development
institutions; (ii) job placement rate of human capital development institutions increased as compared to
pre-project time; (iii) lower rates of hidden and open unemployment as compared to pre-project times; (iv)
lower poverty levels; and (v) higher average incomes in participating communities.
72.   Implementation. A project team will be established in the Structural and Regional Policy
Department of the Ministry of Labor and Social Policy (MOLSP). The project team will be generally
responsible for oversight, monitoring, and provision of technical assistance to ensure implementation of the
labor market surveys and the labor redeployment services at the voivodship, powiat, and gmina levels. Its
primary functions will be to: (a) facilitate procurement of technical assistance and goods, that will be done
through the PCU; (b) facilitate implementation of the labor market information surveys in all voivodships;
(c) following the criteria agreed with the Bank, develop detailed procedures and a management information
system (MIS) for operating the Redeployment Fund and providing technical assistance to Marszalek
Office, powiat, gmina administrations and service providers; (d) maintain the MIS in cooperation with the
- 60 -



VPIUs, and monitor operation of the Redeployment Fund; (d) provide the PCU with regular financial and
program implementation reports. The RSC will approve the replenishment of revolving LF accounts on a
monthly basis, review and approve local labor services provider contracts between US$35,000 and
US$70,000 (contracts over US$70,000 must be sent to the Bank for review and no-objection).
73.   The project team will consist of a minimum of fourteen full time professional staff, of which seven
in Warsaw (i.e., Coordinator, MIS/Accountant, Legal/Contracts, Small Business, Training/Public Works,
Local Economic Development/Community Works, Surveys Coordinator), with support staff, plus one full
time professional staff extension officer stationed in each of the seven voivodship offices, or Marszalek
Offices. The project will provide financing for ten long term consultant staff (including three of the six
central project team staff, and the seven extension agents), related training, plus short-term technical
consultants who are specialists in different Redeployment Fund program areas (e.g. incubator design, local
economic development planning) under an umbrella technical assistance contract. The project team will be
headed by a full-time senior civil servant.
74.   Implementation of Economic and Labor Market Information Surveys. The surveys will be
carried out a minimum of four times in all seven voivodships during the project's implementation period.
Technical assistance, i.e. local and international consultants and training, will be procured by the project
team through the PCU, and made available to the Marszalek Office administration for implementing the
surveys. In the Marszalek Office, the Labor Market Unit will be the primary agency involved with the
technical assistance firm in implementing the surveys and, along with the RDAs, in using the information
generated from the surveys.
75.   Implementation of the Labor Redeployment Services. The fund will be implemented using
simple standard principles and criteria. The key steps in the Redeployment Fund administration are as
follows:
(a)    The MOLSP, in cooperation with the Marszaleks, establishes the algorithm for allocation of the
Redeployment funds by voivodship, and has this approved by the NSC (only 50 percent of the
Redeployment funds will be allocated in the first year)
(b)    The Marszalek Office assigns necessary staff (4-5 people) to deal with publicity, contracting, and
monitoring of labor service contracts. The project team in the MOLPS assigns an extension officer to each
voivodship and provides orientation and training to the Marszalek Office staff in the operation of the
Redeployment Fund
(c)    Each Voivoda Office opens a project account at the Financial Department of the Voivoda Office
(d)    The project team in the MOLPS authorizes the transfer from the Special Account of an initial
US$250,000 to each Financial Department of the Voivoda Office for the implementation of the
sub-component. The Financial Department of the Voivoda Office transfers this amount to the Marszalek
Office project account based on minimum agreed levels of full-time Marszalek Office staff (e.g. three
people) assigned to operate the Redeployment Fund. The initial allocation of US$250,000 can be increased
up to US$500,000 based on monthly payments to local service providers. Payments to service providers
will be made by the Marszalek Office on the basis of contracts signed by the Marszalek Office and
endorsed by the MOLPS project team
(e)    The Marszalek Offices provide publicity to community leaders and potential service providers on
the availability of the Redeployment Fund, and ask powiats (in cooperation with gminas) to submit general
- 61 -



indications of interest in the use of the Redeployment Fund over the next 12 months (e.g. type of programs,
approximate number of people to be served). These proposals will not contain budget estimates as local
officials will not be aware of detailed financing arrangements. The Marszalek Office summarizes these
indications of interest and submits them to the RSC for review and endorsement to ensure consistency of
the proposed programs with regional self-government priorities
(f)    The Marszalek Office, in cooperation with powiat labor offices, will initiate procurement following
Polish Public Procurement Law, to identify service providers (standard public tender notices and sample
contracts, which are contained in the operational manual to be agreed during project negotiations, will be
provided to potential service providers to guide them in developing proposals)
(g)    The Marszalek Office, in consultation with the extension officer, negotiates and executes contracts
with service providers
(h)    The Marszalek Office authorizes agreed advance payments to service providers which initiate
services, report and invoice the Marszalek Office on a monthly basis for services provided. The Marszalek
Office, in cooperation with powiat labor office and the extension agent, monitors contract implementation
(i)    The Marszalek Office provides standard data on each contract (e.g. type of service, service
provider, line item costs, number and type of clients served) to the project team in the MOLPS. The project
team will develop a contract monitoring and evaluation system and database to track contracts with service
providers.
(j)    The Marszalek Office creates a statement of expenses each month, based on invoices paid to
service providers, and submits requests for replenishment of the project account at the Financial
Department of the Voivoda Office to the PCU with copy to the project team in the MOLPS.
76.    Methodology for Identifying Sub-projects. The Redeployment Funds will be available in rural
and urban/rural gminas in the voivodships covered by the RDP. Allocations of funds by voivodship will be
based on an algorithm developed by the MOLSP, in cooperation with the Marszalek Offices, and agreed
with the NSC and the Bank. There will not be any allocation of funds by powiat or gmina within
voivodships, as use of resources will be by demand and need.
77.    Labor redeployment services will be provided to individual citizens through local service providers
selected by public tendering. Eligible individuals include those who are: (a) youth living in the immediate
household of individuals defined under (b), individuals who the Social Welfare or Labor Offices define as
economically disadvantaged, threatened with poverty, needing assistance to upgrade skills, employment,
and/or business opportunities; and (b) individuals who are formally registered as unemployed, have been
served notice that they are going to be released from employment within 90 days, and/or whose sole source
of income is an agricultural plot with three or less counted hectares.
78.    The Redeployment Fund is demand-driven, there is no specific allocation of resources by the
Redeployment Program at the voivodship level. However, gminas and powiats will develop a general plan
for use of the services to be presented to the Marszalek Office and endorsed by the RSC, before
solicitations for individual service provider contracts are begun and related contracts signed by the
Marszalek Office for services. However, the maximum amount of the Redeployment Fund that can be used
in each voivodship is 20 percent for temporary community services.
79.   The operational manual contains eligibility criteria for services, service providers and costs to be
- 62 -



financed under the Redeployment Fund.
80.   Flow of Funds. Project funds will flow to the National Bank of Poland into a Special Account
registered with the MOF. For accounting purposes, this account will have a subsidiary special category for
the Labor Fund, which will reflect the Loan Agreement Schedule of Expenditures. The PCU will take
administrative and fiscal responsibility for project financial and progress reporting, based on input from the
project team in the MOLPS.
81.   Funds for delivery of local labor services financed from the Redeployment Fund will go directly
from the Special Account to a project account at the Financial Department of the Voivoda Office, based on
the authorization of the project team in the MOLPS. It is anticipated that Redeployment Fund allocation by
voivodship will be determined based on an algorithm (e.g. levels of unemployment, population, etc.)
developed by the MOLSP in cooperation with the Marszalek Offices, and will be used to allocate the initial
50 percent of the Redeployment Funds to the voivodships during the first year. The Redeployment Fund at
the voivodship level will be replenished on a monthly basis based on payments made during that month to
local service providers which have signed contracts with the Marszalek Office. Requests for replenishment
of voivodship Redeployment Funds will be routed through the PCU.
82.    Disbursement. The loan will finance 100 percent of relevant technical assistance, 100 percent of
goods (excluding customs and VAT), and 49 percent of labor services delivered by the Redeployment
Fund.
Sub-Component B-2: Education (US$24.67 million).
83.   Sub-component Objective. A key component in the effort to attract new businesses in rural areas
is the implementation of a comprehensive program for the development of a strong education and training
system, capable of providing graduates with the level of knowledge, skills and capacity to learn required by
a modern market economy. The overall objective of the education sub-component is to improve the
efficiency of the education system and the quality of graduates from school education in target gminas by:
(i) enhancing the quality of teaching in rural primary schools and gymnasia; and (ii) improving the
utilization of educational resources.
84.   Tasks. The education sub-component will finance five major activities: (i) a program for
improving the quality of teaching in primary schools and gymnasia in target areas through training; (ii) a
program for improving the quality of school equipment; (iii) a program for supporting the introduction of
computers for educational purposes in rural gminas; (iv) a program for improving school facilities, and
education efficiency, through activities leading to the consolidation of the school network; and (v) support
to project dissemination, implementation, and monitoring.
85.   The implementation of this sub-component will consist of activities that will involve primary
schools and gymnasia in a sub-set of the rural gminas covered by the project. Gminas participating in the
program will be selected based on their capacity to conduct an assessment of the current situation of their
education system, and to prepare a viable proposal to address the main problems and challenges identified
during the assessment. It is expected that the assessment and proposals prepared by these gminas will serve
as examples of good practices to be used in subsequent similar projects.
86.   Program for Improving the Quality of Teaching through Teacher Training (US$5.97 million)
In order to improve teaching and learning in primary schools the project will support the introduction of
new methods of teaching different subjects in an integrated manner. This will be done through: (i) a training
- 63 -



program for teachers in teaching methods and classroom management techniques appropriate for integrated
and multigrade teaching; (ii) a training program for school directors on school supervision, whole-school
planning, school leadership, community participation and mobilization, and education evaluation and
assessment.
87.   The integrated methods of teaching will aim at developing critical thinking skills in graduates from
gymnasium, therefore preparing them for the crucial decisions concerning their future education and
profession. This will significantly affect the composition of the rural labor force in the years to come by
preparing graduates to labor market requirements, and contributing to the diversification of their skills.
88.   The training programs for teachers and school directors will be implemented in two sets of
four-week courses. The courses will involve both classroom as well as practical/hands-on activities. The
training program will be delivered by specialized local training institutions or NGOs, on the basis of
programs approved by local education authorities in collaboration with the Ministry of National Education
(MONE).
89.    Program for Improving the Quality of School Equipment (US$4.39 million). The project will
make funds available to the participating rural gminas to support the work of the newly trained teachers
with educational materials, that will help them put into practice what they have learned.
90.    Program for Supporting the Introduction of Computers for Instructional Purposes in Rural
Gminas (US$4.07 million). This program will support an already existing program that finances the
purchase of computers for schools, and will consist of: (i) a training program for teachers in information
technology; (ii) establishment of a national internet based educational resource center; and (iii) the purchase
of computer software. The teacher training program will be organized through sets of training sessions on
how to use computers as a support to teaching.
91.    Program for Improving School Facilities and Education Efficiency (US$9.97 million). In order
to improve the allocation of resources some rural gminas will have to consolidate their current primary
school network. To support this effort, the project will finance the rehabilitation, upgrading and
refurbishing of some 80 primary schools, selected on the basis of accessibility, crowdedness and school
infrastructure suitability to accommodate the creation of new gymnasia. The project will also support
activities facilitating school consolidation, i.e. improvements in the school transportation system.
92.    Support to project dissemination, implementation, and monitoring (US$0.27 million). To
support the work of the project team in the MONE and the VPIUs, the project will finance eight local
consultants. During the first two years of implementation, it is planned that seven consultants will be
located in each of the VPIUs, and one Managing Consultant will be assigned to the project team in the
MONE. The consultants in the VPIU will report to the Managing Consultant. The general guidance for the
Managing Consultant will be provided by the project coordinator designated by the MONE. The project
will also finance training on project management and procurement for project team members in the MONE
and for VPIU staff members responsible for the education component.
93.    Costs. The total estimated costs of implementing the activities described above are US$24.67
million as described in the table below:

94.   Expected Output. By the end of project's implementation, the targeted gminas will have: (i) better
educated graduates from compulsory education (primary school and gymnasium), who have the capacity to
actively participate in the creation and development of a dynamic private sector in rural areas, and who
have life-long-learning skills required by the democratization of the Polish society and the modernization of
its economy; and (ii) an efficiently run public education system. The project will have trained
approximately twelve thousand teachers and eight hundred school directors in approximately 320 rural
gminas. It is expected that 800 primary schools and gymnasia will benefit from the program for improving
the quality of school equipment. The program of training teachers in information technology will benefit
approximately five thousand teachers working in primary schools and gymnasia in the target rural gminas,
and software will be financed for approximately 530 rural schools. The project will finance the
rehabilitation, upgrading and refurbishing of some 80 selected primary schools, in approximately 60
communities.
95.   Implementation. Three different levels of government will be involved in the implementation of the
project.
96.    National Level. A project team will be established in the Ministry of National Education (MONE).
It will be responsible for defining technical criteria and standards for training programs, instructional mate
rials, educational software, internet based education resource center, school rehabilitation and school
- 65 -



transportation to be financed under the project. The MONE will be responsible for preparing a menu of
options to guide gminas in the preparation of their proposals. Using information provided by regional
authorities, the MONE will conduct periodic assessment of the implementation of the project, and
disseminate best practices. The MONE will have a direct involvement in the development of the internet
site used for distance education. Specifically, the MONE will be responsible for contracting out the
development of the site and the implementation of the program based on TOR agreed with the Bank. The
project team in the MONE will consist of 5-7 representatives of departments responsible for the subject
areas supported by the RDP Education component. The team will be coordinated by a senior civil servant
designated by the MONE. The Undersecretary of State appointed by the Minister of National Education
will be responsible for overall overseeing of its activities. Since the project team members will continue
their current duties, and, therefore, will not be able to work exclusively on a full time basis on the activities
required to implement the education component of the RDP, the project will provide financing for eight
long term local consultants. Seven will be assigned to each of the voivodships participating in the first two
years of the RDP implementation, and one Managing Consultant will be assigned to the project team in the
MONE. Based on the needs, the consultants will share their time between a support to the VPIUs and an
assistance to the MONE in implementing and monitoring the project. The project will also provide the
necessary training to the staff in the project team in the MONE and for the VPIU staff members
responsible for the education component. All consultants will be hired under one umbrella technical
assistance contract. The estimated total cost of consultant services is US$270,000.
97.    Regional Level. The Marszalek's Office through the VPIUs in close collaboration with the office
of the Kurator will be responsible for (i) disseminating the program, providing technical assistance to
gminas, supporting gminas in announcing and evaluating tenders, and monitoring the implementation of the
project to ensure that all eligible gminas are participating in it; (ii) coordinating the implementation of the
training program for teachers, school directors and information technology specialists; and (iii)
coordinating the provision of education materials and school equipment to rural schools. Specifically, this
will include the preparation of bid, evaluation of bid, and issuing of payment orders. Monitoring
information should be shared with the MONE to facilitate the national evaluation of the project. In order to
prepare the dissemination program, VPIUs responsible for managing the project will work in coordination
with the MONE. The RSC will be responsible for evaluating the proposals submitted by gminas. As a
precondition to the submission of proposals, gminas will be asked to present a school network plan
approved by the gmina council and cleared by the Kurator's office. Project proposals presented by gminas
will be required to be consistent with regional development policies and priorities. Joint proposals presented
by two or more gminas will receive preferential consideration during the evaluation process in the form of
extra points.
98.    Local Level. Gminas will be responsible for preparing, in consultation with the local community,
proposals for training teachers, school directors and information technology specialists, and for the
provision of education materials and school equipment. Once the proposal is approved by the RSC, gminas
will be responsible for facilitating its implementation. It is expected that for the implementation of school
rehabilitation and school consolidation, gminas will be directly involved in conducting tenders and signing
contracts. In all other cases, VPIUs will be responsible for procurement, in order to take advantage of
economies of scale (teacher training for example) and to promote collaboration among gminas.
99.    The National Steering Committee in consultation with the project team in the MONE will be
responsible for the initial fund allocation to each voivodship. This allocation will be done based on two
main indicators: (i) an index of resource utilization at the school level estimated using the student teacher
ratio per school; and (ii) an index of overcrowding estimated by using the average square meter of school
facilities per student age population.
- 66 -



100.   The operational manual will provide a general framework for establishing which activities are
eligible for financing, and the technical criteria for the implementation of the activities. Within this
framework the implementation of activities will be done at the local level by local entities such as NGOs,
teacher training institutes or other private contractors, to ensure that they respond to the needs of the target
population and to help develop local capacity and help generate employment.
101.   To effectively reach the target population, this sub-component will be implemented under the direct
supervision of the participating gminas. Foundations, NGOs or local educational institutions will be
involved in the direct execution of project activities. The implementing institutions will be asked to
demonstrate professional expertise in the field, and show understanding of the local community. This will
help ensure that the implemented activities are of high technical quality and respond to the needs of local
communities.
102.   Methodology for Identifying Sub-projects. Investments at the gmina level will be identified
through a competitive process where each of the eligible gminas will be invited to present proposals for
co-financing. Each proposal will be evaluated by the RSC against a set of predefined criteria, and those
approved will be financed as feasible from loan proceeds and matching funds.
103.  To be considered for financing, each education proposal has to reflect a priority for the community,
as shown by local council decisions, the results of any public hearings or beneficiary surveys, and must be
in accordance with the broader, comprehensive program of regional development.
104.  In addition to providing evidence of community support, gminas desiring investments to
consolidate the school network, will be required to conduct: (i) a social assessment of the school
consolidation; and (ii) an economic assessment of different school consolidation options.
105.  In order to provide all eligible gminas with the opportunity to prepare good proposals, the project
will conduct a promotion campaign aimed at informing local policy makers, administrators and
communities about the project. Parallel to this, the project will provide technical assistant to target gminas
to equip them with skills and techniques required for conducting needs assessment and for the preparation
of proposals. Also, gminas will receive technical assistance to help them develop capacity to supervise the
implementation of sub-projects.
106.   Flow of Funds. The flow of funds will follow the scheme presented above for the whole project.
107.  Co-Financing. Funding to support the activities described under the education sub-component will
be provided by the project in the form of grants to gminas. However, participating gminas will be required
to co-finance all education investments contemplated in this sub-component. It is expected that by doing so,
the gminas will have full ownership and commitment to both the objectives and the implementation strategy
of the project. Specifically, the project will use a system of matching grants to finance these activities.
Gminas, with the support of the MONE, will be required to co-finance each activity in the following
proportion: (i) in the case of school consolidation, the project will finance up to a maximum of 42 percent
of total cost; (ii) for training of teachers, school directors, and information technology specialists, the
project will finance up to a maximum of 62 percent of project cost, and for the provision of instructional
materials and school equipment, the project will finance up to a maximum of 59 percent of project cost;
(iii) for computer software, the project will finance up to a maximum of 67 percent of total cost; (iv) for the
establishment of the internet based education resource center, the project will finance up to 75 percent of
total cost; and (v) for the support of project implementation, the project will finance up to a maximum of
- 67 -



81 percent of total cost.
Sub-Component B-3: Institution Building in Local and Regional Administrations (US$12.62 million).
108.   Sub-component Objectives. The overall objective of this sub-component is to increase the level of
efficiency and effectiveness in eligible units of local and regional administration (gminas, powiats and
voivodships) within the voivodships covered by the RDP, through institutional development, training
programs and capacity building measures, and thereby improve the conditions for the creation of non-farm
employment in rural areas. An efficient public administration will improve the provision of goods and
services to the public and the private sectors, thus facilitating economic activities. Most importantly, the
first impulse to overcome the economic stagnation and social apathy can come only in many cases from the
local public administration.
109.   Tasks. The project will finance institutional development programs (IDPs) in selected pilot units to
develop a framework for improving the general efficiency of local administrations, including management
of human and financial resources, and provide TA aiming at improving the quality of services delivered by
local officials and public servants, and build capacity for implementing EU rules and regulations. In
addition, training will be provided to selected employees of self-government administrations operating in
administrative units not benefiting from the IDPs. The training provided will place special emphasis on
public management and administrative services important for the successful implementation of RDP and its
project components. Finally, the project will finance capacity building efforts and studies which will
facilitate the. link between the IDPs and the training programs, foster the coordination with other RDP
components, and provide quality control as well as monitoring and evaluation services.
110.  Institutional development programs, training and capacity building are crucial to the success of a
project aiming at fostering the growth of the private sector. A modern public administration provides
predictable government action, reliable institutional frameworks and regulatory certainty, thus helping the
efficient functioning of the market economy. The better the capacity of the state and self-government
institutions, the better the opportunity for the market economy to work. In addition, public administration
assists market economy by producing sound policies and delivering critical public goods and services in a
cost-effective manner. An efficient public administration is most important for rural areas which are
confronted with the issue of hidden unemployment in agriculture, and urgently require the creation of
non-farming jobs.
111.   Training enables the better use of human resources. It helps people properly discharge the
requirements of their jobs and raises the potential of people to do other, more demanding jobs. In doing so,
training supports organizations and institutions to achieve their objectives. Training can contribute to
change an institution's 'culture,' i.e. the core beliefs, values and attitudes of the employees, thus effecting
the success of the institution. Hence training must be seen as part of the human resource development
strategy, which is in turn part of the strategy for organizational and institutional development. In this
project, the link between institutional development and training will receive special attention in selected
pilot areas.
112.   The decentralization of public services and finances to powiats and voivodships is placing great
demands on public administrators. There are new functions to administer and new processes to apply.
There is the need to coordinate the work among self-governments at different levels, and between
self-governments and the state administration in fields like regional development. Therefore, the state of
preparedness of the public administration at each level becomes crucial for the success of the reform. In
this sense, the IDPs, the training programs and the capacity building efforts will contribute to the project's
- 68 -



overall objective of helping Poland implement the decentralization process. Moreover, this sub-component
will contribute to build the capacity of the local and regional administrators to implement EU regulations
and rules, thus helping Poland to absorb EU pre-accession and structural funds.
113.   This sub-component will provide in parallel three complementary activities:
(a)    Institutional Development Programs (IDPs), focusing on the overall institutional and human
resources development of the public administration in a few selected pilot units at voivodship, powiat and
gmina levels;
(b)    Training Programs, focusing on key generic and project specific issues, offered to all regional and
local administrative units in the project areas; and
(c)    A Capacity Building Program supporting MIAPA in linking IDPs and training activities, including
surveys and studies.
114.  Institutional Development Programs (IDPs) (US$5.12 million). These programs will be
implemented in two voivodships, two to four powiats and about fifteen gminas. The main criterion used in
the selection of the pilot units is their willingness and capacity to quickly improve their performance.
115.   The IDPs will be divided in two stages. During the first six to nine months (stage 1), an
organizational and operational analysis of the pilot units and the design of new institutional arrangements
will be conducted. The analysis will consist of an in-depth assessment of selective organizational and
operational issues in each pilot unit, focusing on departmental structure and tasks, procedures, staffing,
availability and quality of equipment, MIS, division of labor. The result of this analysis will help design
new institutional arrangements to be achieved during stage 11.
116.  During the following two years (stage 11), hand-on assistance will be provided to implement the
suggested organizational changes, design and deliver training packages. As part of the new organizational
structure, new procedures will be drafted, job profiles and task descriptions for key personnel and
departments will be drafted, vacancies will be advertised, the performance assessment of the personnel will
be undertaken, and new equipment and software will be provided.
117.   The success of the IDPs will crucially depend on the commitment of the elected officials and key
public servants to work on the difficult tasks of implementing the institutional improvements. This sense of
ownership needs to be developed during stage I (organizational analysis and design of new institutional
arrangements), and maintained during the whole implementation of the IDPs.
118.  The IDPs, conducted in a limited number of pilot units, will serve as key reference case for the
training programs described below. The lessons learned in the pilot units will guide the selection of trainees,
the choice of training subjects and the methodology of the training to be provided to all administrative units
operating in the project areas.
119.  Training Programs (US$5.10 million). All other administrative units not selected for pilot
operations will be offered training in two sets of subjects: (i) subjects related to the efficiency of public
administration at regional and local levels, and (ii) subjects related to the efficient implementation of RDP
components. The project will provide additional funds to ensure the wide use and application of the new or
updated skills obtained through training, i.e., financing of selected hard and software, and the promotion
and dissemination of relevant experiences and best practices, aimed at developing awareness of the
- 69 -



programs goals among citizens. A menu of options linking the different training topics and the suggested
target groups can be found in the operational manual.
120.   Subiects Related to the Efficiency of Public Administration. This training will cover basic
knowledge in public management, project cycle management, financial management, EU accession
requirements, good governance, etc.
121.   Training in public management will be provided to councilors and board members. With the
reform, decision-makers of the newly created self-government units (powiats and voivodships) face new
administrative responsibilities, often without having the necessary administrative and managerial skills.
Among the most important challenges facing local and regional governments are the satisfaction of
communal needs with limited financial resources; the design and implementation of local and regional
development strategies and programs; and effectively accessing and utilizing aid funds from external
donors.
122.   Public officials will also receive training in project management. Councilors and board members
will need to develop a general understanding of how to prioritize, assess and implement projects.
123.   The training module addressing issues related to financial management will focus on topics such
as: improving public services in the context of limited resources; options for increasing revenues,
decreasing expenditures, and optimizing the combination of different resources (local revenues, central
subsidies, external resources and borrowed funds). This training will be addressed to board members as
well as members of the financial committee, and employees of self-government administrations at higher
and medium levels.
124.   Poland's accession to the EU calls for the creation of EU compatible structures. The introduction
of the 'Law on the Three-level Territorial Division' has been a major step in this direction. A successful
implementation of this law involves however the full understanding of the implications of (future) EU
accession on public services, and related issues such as transparency of budget and tender processes.
Special attention will be given to this topic.
125.   Wherever relevant, training will stress the need and advantages of good governance, i.e. avoiding
conflicts-of-interest, clear division of responsibilities between the politically appointed and the employees,
as well as the cost of and the need to abate corruption.
126.   Subiects Related to the Efficient Implementation of RDP Components. The main focus of training
will be on specific issues related to public services relevant for private sector development, active labor
market measures, rural education, as well as infrastructure. In these priority sectors, decision makers,
senior officers and additional stakeholders will receive training.
127.   Public Administration can play a role in facilitatingprivate sector development by: (i) removing
bottle-necks, and generally improving the business environment; (ii) promoting gminas, powiats and
voivodships for inward investment; (iii) directly providing services, such as information and business space
at competitive conditions. The training program focusing on private sector issues will help operationalize
the topics: (a) provide the regulatory framework that allows markets to work, (b) invest in key
infrastructure to lower private costs of production, (c) use the private sector in financing and managing
public infrastructure, (d) carry out regional and local promotional efforts, and (e) improve delivery and
efficiency of government-produced services of importance to the private sector (e.g. one-stop offices for
business clients).
- 70 -



128.  The main players in implementing active labor programs are the labor offices, the Redeployment
Fund and the private, public and NGO service providers recruited by the Redeployment Fund and the labor
offices. Despite the need to delegate direct measures to designated service providers, there is a role for
Public Administration in: (i) gathering and distributing labor market information; (ii) assessing the work of
the service providers; and (iii) creating a favorable business climate. The 'Law on the Three-level
Territorial Division' assigns a specific role in counteracting unemployment to powiats and voivodship
self-governments. The training to be provided to managers and senior employees in regional and district
labor offices will focus on disseminating best practices and the results of evaluation reports on previous
and ongoing labor programs. As part of the training process managers and senior employees should be
familiarized with: (a) the instruments for the identification and analysis of employment problems at local
and regional levels including databases and in-depth surveys; (b) the principles of active labor market
policies including targeting, localization, prevention, mentoring, outreach, integration and collaboration and
employer involvement; (c) the models of decentralized active labor market policy including regionalized
systems and integrated systems; (d) the current trends in active labor market policy including autonomy in
budget allocation and social partnership; and (e) the implementation of active labor market programs.
129.  Although significant amounts are spent on education at the national level, rural areas are
under-serviced in the area of human capital development. Links between education and the economy are
important; they complement and reinforce the fundamental contribution of education to individual and
social development. Economic activity depends to a growing extent on peoples' knowledge, skills and
capacity to learn continuously. Thus investment in education is important for economic growth and national
competitiveness. With the education and administrative reforms, regional and local self-governments are
responsible for both education management and finance at their respective statutory levels - early childhood
and primary education for gminas, secondary education for powiats, and tertiary education for voivodships
- and must primarily finance expenditures from their own revenues. Training under this component will
focus on assisting the education offices in the gmina and powiat administrations to improve management of
the limited budget resources mainly through increasing the efficiency of public schools.
130.  In the physical infrastructure sector, sorting out the planning, financial, operating and
maintenance responsibilities at the various levels of government and the private sector will be necessary for
effective management of infrastructure stocks and new investments, including the efficient use of local,
national and international funds. Possible training topics include: (i) at the voivodship level, the planning of
regional infrastructure needs, and monitoring and enforcing national standards on municipal service
facilities, and (ii) at the powiat gmina level, engineering economy, the planning of current and future needs
of physical infrastructure, the operation and maintenance of roads, service facilities and buildings, and
basic rules for public consultation and social assessment methods.
131.  Improving the environment by complying with environmental national and EU regulations is
important for all regions in Poland, and not only for those that have opted to invest in tourism. Issues of
environmental protection will be addressed in all training sessions where potentially relevant, i.e. project
cycle management, infrastructure management, regional development and even private sector development.
132.  Training Methodology. The range of possible training methods to be considered under this
sub-component includes training on-the-job, in-house-training, workshops, computer-based training, and
distance learning. The choice of a specific method will depend on the training subject and participants.
133.   Target Groups. The training activities will target different groups including officers, board
members and councilors at the gmina, powiat and voivodship levels. The training will therefore need to be
- 71 -



flexible and adapt to the needs of the trainees.
134.  Specific training focusing on the transfer of technical skills should in principle be addressed to
public servants at the high and intermediary levels. Although management and organization in general do
not concern elected councilors, it is nevertheless necessary to create in this group a level of understanding
on managerial issues, since approval from them is required for any organizational development (e.g.
introduction of a new structure). Board members need training in managerial skills. This training should
however have a practical and applicable character, with a minimum of lectures and a maximum of role
plays and case-studies. The accepted training method should reflect the different educational levels,
background and different professional experiences of this target group. A special training program is
envisaged for secretaries of gminas, powiats and voivodships, since their responsibilities usually include
important aspects of office organization.
135.  Capacity Building and Studies (US$2.40 million). The institutional development and training
programs included in the RDP are ambitious and innovative, as well as complex. Implementation of the two
programs therefore calls for careful coordination and intensive monitoring. Optimum results cannot be
ensured without systematic interaction between the service providers of the institutional development and
training programs, and without continuous adaptation of the two programs in view of the lessons learned.
In order to ensure that in changing circumstances which currently cannot be foreseen, the service providers
of the IDPs and training programs will properly implement the project, active guidance and continuous
support are needed. This kind of support and guidance would naturally be expected from the Ministry of
Interior and Public Administration (MIAPA). In order to make MIAPA capable of performing this role, it
is necessary to: (i) strengthen human resources within MIAPA, and (ii) create organizational structures for
the effective and sustainable coordination and support of activities aimed at developing local and regional
administration especially in rural areas. Accordingly, the Capacity Building program is designed to assist
MIAPA in (i) efficiently co-ordinating the IDPs and training programs; (ii) disseminating the
accomplishments of the IDPs; and (iii) providing the tools and means to support the IDPs in the local and
regional administration.
136.  Studies will be financed to evaluate the success of the sub-component. The evaluation of the IDP
will be done through a comprehensive evaluation audit that will assess the degree of institutional
development achieved at the end of the project against the benchmarks developed during stage I of the IDP.
The training programs will be evaluated using three tools: (i) periodic beneficiaries assessments, in the form
of participants reactions recorded by questionnaires and rating scales; (ii) a client survey run towards the
end-of project implementation; and (iii) the quantitative information collected in the MIS during the life of
the project, such as average training hours per employee, and training costs per participant hour. In
addition, the project will finance a study on distance learning.
137.   Flow of Funds. Founds will flow according Polish regulations, i.e. the Law on Public Finance.
138.  Costs. The technical assistance and support provided under the IDP is estimated at US$5.12
million. The cost of the training courses, office equipment and promotion and dissemination campaign
provided in all the participating administrative units will amount to US$5. 10 million. The costs of the
capacity building and studies are estimated at US$2.40 million. The total cost for this sub-component is
estimated at US$12.62 million.

139.   Expected Output The expected outcome is a significant contribution to the development of a
framework needed for improving the management of human and financial resources in regional and local
administrations, the provision of training to some 3,000 decisions makers and senior staff in the pilot and
other administrative units for an average of 30 days of training per trainee, and a significantly increased
capacity at the central government level to provide guidance and support to regional and local
administrative units, as well as to monitor and evaluate such support programs.
140.  Three key accomplishments, described below containing both quantitative and qualitative elements,
are proposed as the main evaluation criteria to be used at the end of the project. The accomplishments are
the most significant indicators for a successful implementation of this sub-component. These triggers
(i) A beneficiaries assessment and a client survey conducted towards the end of the project in gminas,
powiats and voivodships participating in the IDP indicates a perceived increase in the efficiency of how
public administration is conducted (i.e. efficient use of available human and financial resources).
(ii) At least 3,000 decision-makers and officers operating at gmina, powiat and voivodship levels will have
received an average of 30 days of training.
(iii) The relevance and quality of the training provided, evaluated through a variety of tools and measures,
will be judged satisfactory.
Project Component 3 - US$ 194.89 million
Component C: Rural Infrastructure (US$194.89 million).
141.  Component Objectives. The development and improvement of infrastructure is regarded as a
prerequisite for stimulating private sector development. Areas with developed infrastructure attract
- 73 -



investors, whereas areas with inadequate infrastructure place a burden of additional costs on potential
investors, who may need to build roads, water supply, waste water collection, access to district heating,
telecommunication, etc., in order to start and operate a new business. The objective of this component is to
improve technical infrastructure in rural areas, in order to stimulate private sector investments, facilitate
the creation of non-farm jobs, improve environmental and health conditions, introduce alternative
organizational and institutional structures for the sustainable delivery of affordable services, introduce
more market oriented approaches in the development and operation of infrastructure networks, thus
contributing to narrow the gap between rural and urban areas in economic development.
142.  Tasks. Within this component, investments will be considered to address the following
infrastructure needs: (i) water supply systems so as to provide reliable water for domestic and commercial
use; (ii) sewage collection and treatment facilities, often in conjunction with water supply systems so as to
complete the cycle of reliable and hygienically acceptable water systems for the benefit of rural enterprises
and the welfare of rural citizens; (iii) solid waste management systems, including collection, treatment, and
disposal facilities in order to fulfill legal, safety and sanitary requirements; (iv) selected rural roads, most
likely for improvements such as local linkages to new motorways and surface hardening in order to provide
all weather access to certain communities. Based on the sub-project proposals which were submitted (see
investment portfolio), the average size of a rural infrastructure investment financed under the RDP is
estimated at US$460,000. About 60 percent of the investments will cost less than US$260,000, and 90
percent less than US$1.3 million.
143.  Investment Portfolio. The process for selecting sub-projects to be financed under this component
follows the criteria described below in the chapter on implementation arrangements. In order to develop a
project pipeline for rapid implementation of the first set of investments, participating self-governments
(gmina, associations of gminas, powiats, voivodships) were invited to send their list of high priority
investment projects to a team of consultants in the form of an application for financial support. Only
investments were considered which were ready for immediate implementation including feasibility studies,
financial and technical documentation and all required permits. The task was organized on a regional level
and supported by the Marszaleks. The voivodship self-government provided funding for two consultants in
each voivodship. In addition, the portfolio preparation was supported by consultants identified and selected
by the Bank, and financed through a Dutch Trust Fund. In April 1999, the consultants presented the
outcome.
144.  The rural infrastructure component will cover all sixteen voivodships. The allocation of funds
between the different voivodships is the responsibility of the NSC which will produce methodology for
allocation of funds. Seven voivodships, i.e. Malopolskie, Podkarpackie, Swietokrzyskie, Lubelskie,
Warminsko-Mazurskie, Kujawsko Pomorskie, and Zachodnio-Pomorskie already have the necessary
capacity to implement RDP. Over 1,000 decision-makers participated in the seminars and were introduced
to the objectives and procedures of the RDP. In total, 2,874 project proposals were submitted, of which
1,051 are ready for immediate implementation for a total investment of US$488.3 million. About 41
percent of this amount (US$202.6 million) is requested from the Bank loan. Based on a primary review of
the proposals undertaken by the Polish consultants, it can be assumed that the proposals are in general
overestimated by 10 to 30 percent. However, the proposals show that local governments identify their main
need for investments in the services of water and waste water, and rural roads (see table 5 and 6). Low
demand is indicated by local government for rural telecommunication (0.8 percent), and eligible energy
projects (1.3 percent). Therefore RDP-finance is limited to investments in the water, waste water, roads and
solid waste sector. Since RDP is demand-driven, the RSCs will review after one year of implementation the
need to add new sub-sectors on the basis of requests from local self-governments. As soon as the local
ARMA offices and the VPIUs are in place the proposals will be screened to check if they meet criteria for
- 74 -



financing.

145.  Training of Technical Staff (US$1.11 million). The main concern is the
optimization of the infrastructure investments in relation to the objectives of employment
generation, economic growth, amelioration of the environment, economy and efficiency.
There are several obstacles to achieving this aim through a program of rural infrastructure
investments largely conceived and designed at the gmina level. These are:
1)    The lack of a tradition of engineering design, which emphasizes rate of return, economies of scale,
location economics and logistics, consideration of operating costs per unit of usage, phasing of investments
in line with projected demand, and constant pursuit of new cheaper technologies to achieve desired goals.
2)     The arbitrary technical standards of design, which increase the costs while yielding little actual
benefit.
3)     The boundaries of the fairly small gminas. If the design of investments is pursued looking only
- 75 -



within the gmina boundaries, important benefits will be lost. Many of the most successful developments in
rural telecommunications, sanitation and pollution control in Poland today involve leagues, federations, or
cooperatives of gninas grouped around physical investment programs. This trend will be accelerated by the
project.
4)     Local politics is a threat to the optimization of rural investments. The best antidote to this threat,
and to all the other obstacles to engineering and economic rationality, is a thorough and pervasive
professionalism of the individuals who must conceive and design the proposed investments.
146.   This professionalism will be sought through training of such individuals in a setting where they will
meet and engage with their counterparts, from other gminas in their voivodship, and gain a practical
understanding of the principles of engineering economy as outlined above. The training will be reinforced
and deepened by inspection visits and project reviews done by carefully recruited experts at the voivodship
level, whose mission will include improving the quality of gmina engineers and accountants by working
together to refine project proposals.
147.   To achieve the objectives described above, a comprehensive training and technical assistance
program in rural infrastructure is proposed under the project. The proposed training program will target
self-government officials and relevant technical staff. This includes mayors, members of gmina councils,
staff of investment departments in gmina offices, and technical staff from utilities and service providers will
be encouraged to participate in such training. The objectives of the training workshops and seminars are: i)
to increase awareness of public sector officials regarding alternative approaches for the delivery of public
services, ii) to increase effectiveness, iii) to improve service quality and level, iv) to reduce cost and subsidy
requirements, and v) to improve affordability. The training program of self-government officials is
presented and financed under the B-3 component.
148.   Training sessions for each of the following sub-sectors which will be supported by the project
(water and sewer, roads, solid waste) will be presented covering various topics in a 2.5 day seminar,
including but not limited to:
(i) Infrastructure finance and development: methods and techniques for planning and financing of
municipal infrastructure including capital investment planning, project preparation and management and
technical and financial feasibility of infrastructure projects and application of appropriate design standards.
(ii) Operations and management practices to improve efficiency of services.
(iii) Case studies on best practices from Poland and other countries in each sector.
149.  It is estimated that the total cost of the proposed training is US$ 1.11 million. This will include
training sessions in the sixteen voivodships in Poland.
150.   Technical Assistance for VPIU Staff and Local Offices of ARMA Staff (US$1.09 million) In
addition to the training program, a technical assistance program for the VPIUs and local offices of ARMA
is proposed. The TA program will provide assistance in projects review, and thereby provide hands-on
transfer of know-how to the VPIUs and local offices of ARMA staff on best practices from Poland and
abroad. Local offices of ARMA staff, with aid from Polish consultants, will review technical proposals
received from gminas, and through this process sharpen the skills of gmina staff regarding project
evaluation, review, and appraisal.
- 76 -



151.  The technical support program is designed to transfer experience from other countries, which have
either undergone similar decentralization of service delivery systems to the local governments, and/or have
a long tradition of delivering services by local governments. Therefore, a modest input from a foreign
consultant will be supplemented by Polish professionals with international experience. It is envisaged that
Polish and international consultants will provide necessary transfer of know-how to the VPIU and local
offices of ARMA staff to ensure long term sustainability of the project.
152.  Local governments in rural areas have limited capacity in identifying and prioritizing their
investment needs. This will require that the VPIUs provide necessary support to the gminas and local
governments in this process. Such assistance will include, but it will not limited to providing: a) support in
writing consultant TORs for specific studies required by the gminas; b) assisting in the procurement
process; c) support in supervision of various program implementation. In providing such assistance, VPIUs
will rely on its own staff as well as its consultants. Estimated total cost for the TA is US$1.09 million, in
addition a workshop for the technical staff in the VPI Us and the local government officials will be
organized and the cost is estimated at US$0.22 million.
153.  Monitoring and Evaluation (US$0.21 million). Early monitoring of the implementation and the
evaluation of the project's impact and cost is regarded as a key element for the success of the RDP. In
addition, a comprehensive evaluation study (US$0.21 million) concerning the implementation of the
project, quality of investments, capacity building, environmental and social implications, and economic
impact will be accomplished towards the end of project's implementation. The monitoring activities are
accomplished by the VPIUs and financed under its budget.

154.   Expected Output. The component will result in (i) investments of about US$177.39 million for
improved and developed rural infrastructure, and (ii) better quality and efficiency of rural infrastructure
services.
- 77 -



155.  Implementation. The rural infrastructure component will be implemented at the regional and local
level. The national administrative structure will be involved in coordinating and monitoring activities. The
implementation scheme reflects the decentralization reform launched on January 1, 1999, which gives
gmina, powiat and voivodship self-government the responsibility for the development of rural infrastructure
as well as of Poland's preparation to absorb EU's SAPARD pre-accession fund.
156.  National Level. A project team will be established in the MARD jointly together with the MOE.
This team will be cooperating at the central level with the PCU, which has the overall coordination function
for the RDP. In addition, the PCU will be responsible for the launching of the RDP, procuring the TA and
training services, and for providing assistance to all level of project management.
157.  Regional Level. The Marszalek's Office through the VPIUs in close collaboration with the RSC
will be responsible for disseminating the program, providing technical assistance and training to gminas,
supporting gminas in announcing and evaluating tenders, and monitoring the implementation of the project
to ensure that all eligible gminas are participating in it. Monitoring information should be shared with the
project team in MARD and MOE to facilitate the national evaluation of the project. Local offices of
ARMA will review the project proposals submitted by local governments according to technical and
institutional requirements as defined in the Operational Manual. The VPIUs will review the project
proposals to check for compliance with regional, social and economic development priorities. ARMA has
no approval power, and after evaluating the proposals, the local offices of ARMA will send the
documentation to the VPIU/RSC with copy to the applicant. To ensure the efficient evaluation of
proposals, by the end of March 2000, the local offices of ARMA will need to have the capacity to assess
the economic, financial, environmental and technical quality of projects, and a financial management
system satisfactory to the Bank. Finally the RSCs will be responsible for projects prioritization taking into
account the above-mentioned criteria. The RSCs will be responsible for project prioritization based on the
broader regional economic development plan. As a precondition to the submission of proposals,
self-governments will be asked to contribute to 30 percent of the total investment costs. Sub-project
proposals will be required to be consistent with regional development policies and priorities, as well as
national sector policies. The principle of economies of scale has to be incorporated in the sub-projects
design. Joint proposals presented by two or more gminas will receive preferential consideration during the
evaluation process.
158.  Local Level. Gminas will be responsible for preparing high priority proposals in consultation with
the local comnmunity and, once approved by the RSC, implementing them. It is expected that gminas will be
directly involved in conducting tenders, signing and supervising contracts. Within this framework, the
implementation of activities will be done at the local level to help develop local capacity and generate
employment. The implementing institutions will be asked to demonstrate professional expertise in the field.
This will help ensure the quality of the investments.
159.  The responsibilities of the various entities involved in the project implementation were confirmed
with the borrower during appraisal, and are summarized in the table 8.

160.   Methodology for Selecting Sub-projects. The selection of sub-projects, as detailed in the
- 79 -



Operational Manual, will be accomplished in three phases, including:
Phase A:      Eligibility check
Phase B:      Quality review
Phase C:      Project prioritizing
161.   Phase A, Eligibility Check. The proposals have to meet the following eligibility criteria: (i) the
infrastructure investment is located in an area targeted by the RDP; (ii) the financing is limited to
construction, rehabilitation, replacement, improvement or expansion of service assets in water supply
systems, sewage collection and treatment, solid waste management systems and rural roads; (iii) the
proposal is in compliance with the objectives of the RDP; (iv) the proposal is submitted by an eligible
applicant (gmina, association of gminas, powiat); (v) the self-government contributes a minimum of 30
percent of the total investment of which 10 percent should be financed by a upfront contribution from the
users.
162.   The proposals will need to be accompanied by a decision of the respective local government
council, and for voivodship proposals of the Sejmik. The local offices of ARMA and VPIUs will review the
proposals, and will reject only those that clearly fall outside the project eligibility criteria. The VPIU will
request the beneficiaries to provide additional information if necessary. All eligible projects which are ready
for implementation - including the full financial and technical documentation as well as all required permits
- will enter the project pipeline.
163.   Phase B, Quality Review. Beneficiaries will be encouraged to secure funding from sources like the
EU pre-accession funds (SAPARD and Phare), the National and Regional Environmental Protection Funds,
the EcoFund, and various other national and regional funds, before submission of projects proposals; or at
least by the time of project prioritization. The RSC will only approve projects with fully secured financing.
Investment proposals will be reviewed by the local offices of ARMA against technical, financial, and
institutional requirements:
(i) Community support. Infrastructure investments considered here will reflect a high priority of the
community, as evidenced by local council decisions, the results of any public hearings or beneficiary
surveys, and will be in accordance with a broader, comprehensive program of regional development. Public
hearings are especially required for new investments in waste water treatment and landfills. Gminas and
their utilities should exercise full ownership of the sub-project, by making independent investment choices
and taking responsibility for sub-project success and failure.
(ii) Technical and environmental standards. Investments should comply with Polish and EU technical and
environmental standards and regulations. In addition, the investments should be supported by appropriate
feasibility studies, of a depth that is in line with the sub-project's size and complexity, demonstrating that
the sub-project meets a prudently assessed demand in a cost-efficient way. If a least cost solution is not
selected, adequate justification must be provided. The investments should be determined primarily on the
basis of regional and local needs, and fit within EU and national sector policies.
(iii) Financial feasibility. Investments should be evaluated based on an appropriate financial analysis.
Alternative designs and solutions should be considered, with cost effective use of scarce financial resources
and employment generating efficiency as guiding principles for selection. Capacity to finance adequate
ongoing operations and maintenance must be demonstrated. Investments should generate an Economic
Internal Rate of Return (EIRR) higher than 10 percent. Models for the economic and financial analysis of
rural infrastructure investments were developed for the RDP, financed by the British Know How Fund.
- 80 -



Training for the users of the manuals will be provided in the early stage of implementation.
(iv) Tariffs. For revenue generating infrastructure services, a tariff will be applied to recover the costs of
full O&M and debt service, as well as to include the depreciation of the new investment, and to protect
against the effect of inflation. Where the infrastructure investment is tied to tariff increases for utility
services, the applicant must demonstrate a commitment and ability to increase the tariff to the required
level. In the case that the cost recovery requirement may result in a tariff which is not affordable, the gmina
will have the option to start with a tariff covering the cost of full O&M and debt service, and gradually
introduce a "full cost recovery" tariff over a period of 5 years. This exception from the full cost recovery
principle is limited to sewerage and waste water treatment investments. The project should not lead to tariff
increases of such scale as to make utility services unaffordable, taking into account other local services and
living costs. Gminas are not expected to conduct comprehensive willingness-to-pay studies. However, it is
required that the Gmina indicates the social impacts of the investment and how the affordability of the tariff
is assessed .
(v) Institutional capacity and appropriateness of service delivery organizations. The beneficiary should be
financially viable and should have sufficient institutional capacity and appropriate structure in place to
ensure sustainable operation and maintenance (O&M) of project investments. The assessment of the
institutional capacity is the responsibility of the local offices of ARMA.
(vi) Readiness. Sub-projects should start with a clear and complete financing plan, including evidence that
any co-financing proposed has or will be secured on time. Sub-projects can be approved only when all
necessary permits (i.e. planning, construction, environment) and required legal documents (i.e. title on land)
are available.
164.   Based on the criteria described, the local offices of ARMA will review project proposals and
submit recommendations to the VPIUs, that in turn will assess the quality of the sub-projects proposals in
line with the regional development objectives and submit the evaluation to the RSCs.
165.   Phase C, Project Prioritization. The RSC established a prioritized list of sub-projects for RDP
financing which was presented and discussed during appraisal. The following criteria were used by the
RSC for the ranking: (i) importance for the broader regional economic development plan; (ii) potential for
direct and indirect job creation; (iii) joint proposal among gminas which reflects the principle of economy
of scale in project design; (iv) contribution of self-government to investment cost.
166.   The process of project prioritization and funding commitment will be carried out once or twice per
year, taking into account the amount of time required for identifying and preparing new sub-projects.
167.   The selection and appraisal criteria as described above were discussed with the active participation
of representatives of the Borrower and likely participating institutions. The set of criteria for rural
infrastructure investments were finalized during a workshop held in Warsaw July 22, 1999 jointly together
by the MOE, MARD, RSC and Marszaleks of the relevant voivodships and the Bank.
168.   Flow of Funds. Funds will flow according to the Polish Public Finance Law, as presented in the
scheme for the whole project.
169.   Co-financing. The infrastructure sub-projects will be funded from the following sources: (a) a
beneficiary (local government) contribution of a minimum of 30% of the total investment cost (a minimum
10% of the project costs should be collected as capital charges from the final beneficiaries); (b) World
- 81 -



Bank funds provided by the national government to local governments as grants up to 30% for water
supply; and 50% for other infrastructure sub-projects. The WB contribution will be reduced by the same
percentage of which the project receives grant funding from other sources. This means that the total grant
portion for eligible projects is limited to 30 percent for water projects and 50 percent for waste water, roads
and solid waste projects; (c) contribution from regional or national Environment Funds, Eco Fund and
NGOs on a grant or loan basis; and (d) loans to the local governments from commercial bank. Technical
assistance and training (consultancy services) will be funded 100% by Bank funds.
170.  During the first year of project's implementation, EU pre-accession funds are expected to become
available to participating self-governments for infrastructure investments, EU SAPARD funds on a
reimbursement basis for all sixteen voivodships, and EU Phare funds for some voivodships on a
co-financing or parallel financing basis with RDP. These funds are expected to become available in early
2000. Based on discussions with EU authorities and the Polish implementing entities, common project
approval mechanisms will have to be adopted and applied.
Project Component 4 - US$3.77 million
Component D: Project Management (USD$3.77 million).
171.  The project will also finance the costs of the PCU (equipment, staff and O&M), and a provision is
made for the costs incurred by the project teams in the line ministries and the VPIUs. The description of the
functions of each member of the PCU is in annex I of the operational manual. The breakdown of these
