Project               Bulgaria: Regional Initiatives Fund Project
(Mary Beth Schmidt - Task manager)
Developmental         The projects development objective is to test the social fund
Objective of the      mechanism as a means of improving the standards of living amongst
Project               the poor and unemployed during economic transition.
Project Components   I. Microprojects US$ 4.7 million
II. Labor Market Analysis (LMA) - US$0.4 million
III. Project management US$ 1.  million
The total project cost is US$ 6.3 million. The Bank will finance
US$4.9 million or 77% of the total project cost.
Number of             Newly Created Project Management Unit (PMU - members recruited
Implementing          by the MLSP Ministry of Labor and Social Policy) which is
Agencies              supposed to be develop into an independent government agency after
the 24-months period
(during the fist 18 months UNDP will provide technical assistance
UNDP's support service role is limited to: assistance with reporting
requirements, direct payments, recruitment of project personnel,
organization of training activities, and procurement of goods and
services.)
(LMA carried out by the statistical National Statistical Institute)
A Steering Committee of Government and NGO representatives has
been established to oversee the activities of the PMU with a
composition and terms of reference acceptable to the Bank. In
addition to approving micro-projects and providing guidance and
oversight to the PMU, the SC will endorse (i) financial audits, (ii)
quarterly progress reports and financial statements, (iii) any changes
to the Operational Manual for the RIF-LIL.
- 168 -



Pattern of Project     Microprojects will be proposed and implemented by "Intermediaries",
Organization           that is municipalities, NGOs, cooperatives and other civil society
organizations with the legal status that would enable them to sign
contracts, open bank accounts, spend public money and have the
authority over a microproject facility/infrastructure. Duties and rights
are listed in the Operational Manual. Their responsibilities specific to
each microproject would be stipulated in a Funding Agreement signed
by the PMU and the Intermediary.
Detailed procedures are described in the Operational Manual to
promote, appraise, prioritize, approve, implement, supervise and
evaluate microprojects.
Preparation, Appraisal and Approval
Intermediaries will be encouraged during a country-wide promotion
campaign to identify microprojects and submit Preliminary
Application Forms (PAF) to the PMU. The PMU screens the PAFs
against exclusive criteria. Those that pass the exclusive criteria are
ranked by "need" by using prioritizing criteria. The PMU will make
field visits to about 120 of the microprojects with the highest need
score. After an assessment of the social, institutional, environmental,
economic, financial and technical feasibility of the microproject, the
PMU will authorize Intermediaries to contract a consultant to prepare
the drawings, bill of quantities, activities schedule, technical studies
or other prerequisites for approval. These costs will be calculated in
the total cost of the microproject.
Upon receipt of the required preparation documents, the PMU and/or
technical consultants may conduct a second field visit to complete the
assessments. The microprojects will be scored again taking into
account firm estimates of costs and labor content that will be
available after preparation and appraisal. Microprojects approved by
the PMU and estimated to cost US$40.000 and above, and the first
ten microprojects irrespective of cost, will require approval by the
Steering Committee prior to implementation.
Flow of Funds          The MOF signed the loan agreement, the money is channeled through
UNDP into a special account which is disbursed in Sofia. A local
account is established by the PMU. The PMU receives requests for
payment from contractors with the agreement from the Municipal
Council/NGO. The PMU authorizes payment to the contractor. The
loan money does not flow through the municipalities, but they receive
grants to prepare microprojects (for e.g. water tests, feasibility tests).
Based on experience about how municipalities deal with those grants
they may get more responsibilities.
- 169 -



Procurement Methods   A funding Agreement between the Intermediary and the PMU will be
signed following approval of the microproject, describing the duties
and liabilities of all parties, technical specifications, budget,
procurement methods and contracting procedures. The Intermediary
will procure goods, services and works for microprojects in
compliance with the Operational Manual, with guidance and
oversight by the PMU. The Operational Manual will detail the steps
to be followed and coordination arrangements to ensure
Intermediaries can participate in procurement while maintaining
compliance with World Bank procurement guidelines. The
Intermediary will enter into a contract with the winning
bidder/supplier, using a standard contract provided by the PMU.
Payment to the contractor/supplier/consulting service will be in
parallel with progress achieved and only after the Intermediary and
PMU verifies that the work, services and goods are satisfactory.
Local and National     Spelled out in detail in the OM
Rules and Regulations
such as
Environmental Laws
etc.
Democratic Decision    Introduction of democracy has led to considerable decentralization of
Taking Process where   administrative functions in municipalities. Mayors and Municipal
Stakeholders are       Councils are elected and undertake their functions by using local
Taken into Account    taxes/fees and central subsidies.
RIF-LIL integrated the following ideas: (i) the Municipal Council is a
forum in which microprojects can be debated and endorsed, (ii) press
coverage of council meetings inforns residents of decision making,
(iii) in each municipality, a Technical Committee will act as an
inter-agency coordination body to ensure that microprojects are
consistent with sector plans and norms, (iv) technical assistance is
needed to assist municipalities in preparation of microprojects and
procurement of works; and (v) a funding agreement specifying the
responsibilities and rights of the municipalities and the PMU is
needed to empower the intermediaries and hold them accountable.
- 170 -



Evaluation of the      No evaluation is as yet available, but monitoring and evaluation
Project if available   arrangements are part of the design in order to evaluate data from
experiences made with the RIF-LIL
Monitoring and Evaluation Arrangements: The PMU is responsible
for feedback on the implementation and the impact of the
microprojects on the basis of recommendations on the RIF's design
and regulations. To enable the PMU to estimate costs and benefit of
microprojects, so that comparisons can be made with other programs,
an integrated monitoring and evaluation system will facilitate learning
and project supervision. This consists of microproject monitoring; a
computerized Management Information System and evaluations
including a beneficiary assessment and impact assessment.
Current Status of the    The LIL was approved on November 20, 1998. The expected closing
project                date is April, 30, 2001.
Other interesting      Performance indicators: Since the Government's chief motivation
features               for developing the RIF is to create income earning opportunities for
vulnerable groups, the impact of the microprojects financed by the
LIL will be judged against this objective. In particular, indicators will
focus on microprojects as (i) a more cost-effective means to transfer
income to vulnerable groups than existing social assistance programs;
and ii) as a more effective and efficient instrument for employment
creation than existing ALMPs run by the Government.

Project                 Moldova Social Investment Fund Project (MSIF)
Thomas Blinkhorn - Task Manager
Developmental           The two project development objectives are: (i) help empower rural
Objective of the Project   communities by strengthening their decision making capacity (ii)
improve the quality of basic social and economic services for rural
populations in Moldova, particular for the poor. The SIF provides
a new model of community-based development, and offers a
modest, first opportunity to those who have suffered
disproportional from the economic transition.
Project Components      1. Improved Delivery of Basic Services (US$16.7 million)
II. Strengthened Children's Social Development (US$5 million)
111. Capacity Building for Community and Local Government
(US$2 million)
IV. Project Management Unit (US$2.9 million)
The total project cost is US$20.3. The Bank will finance US$14.8
million or 73% of the total project cost.
Number of               MSIF/PMU, Implementing Agency (IA), Private Contractors and
Implementing Agencies    Local Governments
- 173-



Pattern of Project      MOF will pass on the IDA credit to the MSIF as a grant to finance
Organization            microprojects implemented directly by community beneficiary
groups.
The community is requested to attend promotional meetings,
organize into an elected body (Implementation Agency), complete a
microproject application, raise 15% of total project cost,
competitive procure works and services, and supervise the
implementation and future operation and maintenance of the
facility/program. The MSIF provides promotion and information
on choices, technical assistance throughout the microproject cycle,
supervision oversight, and monitoring and evaluation. The MSIF
will enter into performance contracts with Implementing Agencies,
or newly created Beneficiary Associations, to provide incentives
(through a 2-year matching grant arrangement) to sustain the
quality of the microproject service post-investment.
MSIF has drafted a project implementation plan that includes a
4-year implementation schedule detailed project cost tables and the
final MSIF Operational guidelines (OG). The Operational
guidelines, with accompanying handbooks on finance and
administration, and microproject promotion, appraisal, and
follow-up/supervision, have been refined on lessons learned during
the pilot project. The OG clearly specify processes, procedures,
roles and responsibilities for project implementation, and offer one
of several tolls for project transparency and accountability. The
OG will be adapted in the Operational Manual (OM).
Flow of Funds           MOF will pass on the IDA credit to the MSIF as a grant to finance
microprojects implemented directly by community beneficiary
groups.
Procurement Methods    For works above US$100,00 NCB, for goods IS for contracts up
to US$200,000 and NS up to US$50,000 and for consultant
services BCBSICQ
Democratic Decision     The community- based groups, referred to as local implementation
Taking Process where    agencies are responsible for microproject implementation. The
Stakeholders are Taken    group is elected during the general community meeting to represent
into Account            the community, and typically includes five members, two of whom
must be women. The beneficiary communities are expected to
organize itself through these LAs, to identify and to reach
consensus on small-scale investment priorities which maximize
public benefit, and take responsibility for implementation.

Current Status of the   Since November 1997, the Moldova SIF has been implementing a
Project                 US$1.4 million pilot project. The project was appraised in
September 1998 and went to the board on January 28, 1999.
Evaluation of the       N/A
Project if available
Other interesting       The MISF pilot and other SIFs in the ECA region provided highly
features of the project    the following useful lessons for the design of the main project: (iO
the importance of maintaining an autonomous PMU to depoliticize
the microproject process and ensure effective targeting; (ii) the
advantage of recruiting competitively at market prices for PMU
staff; iii) the composition of the SC or Board, where possible,
should a) include central ministries but avoid line ministries in
order to minimize the influence over microproject types and b)
include 50% government and 50% non-government representatives;
iv) the advantage of investing in a pilot phase to tailor the SIF to
specific country context; and v) the need to focus upstream, with
TA and training, on community organization, strong participation,
and financial contribution.
